The Impossibility of Two Motions in One Particle
Nasafi states Hisham's claim and gives the first dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's initial argument that a particle cannot have two motions because either it exits its location by one motion or not, leading to a contradiction.

Core Idea
Two motions for one particle are impossible because each motion would either move it or not.

Hisham ibn Amr, a Mu'tazili, claimed that each particle of a stone has two motions from two agents. Nasafi begins his refutation by examining whether the particle actually changes location with each motion. This lesson presents the initial dilemma.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the claim and the first argument.
2
Identify the dilemma
Notice that the argument presents two cases: either the particle exits its location by one motion or not.
If it exits, the other motion is redundant; if it does not, it is not a motion.
3
Understand the term 'exiting location'
Motion is defined as leaving a location. If a motion does not cause exit, it is not a real motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم هشام بن عمرو أن كل جزء من أجزاء الحجر يحصل فيه حركتان أحداهما فعل لهذا والأخرى فعل لذلك، وهذا محال، لأن الجزاء إن كان يخرج بأحديهما عن المكان الأول فالأحرى إذا لم تخرج بها عن المكان الأول فلا تكون حركة، وإن كان لا يخرج بأحديهما عن المكان الأول فهى ليست بحركة. فإن قال: يخرج بأحديهما إذا انفردت وبهما إذا اجتمعت. قلنا: إذا خرج الجزء بهما عن المكان الأول أخرج بهما جميعًا أم بأحديهما أم بكل واحد منهما؟ فإن قال : خرج بهما جميعًا فهما جميعًا علة واحدة فكانت كل واحدة منهما بعض العلة وهو باطل، لأنها لم تكن حركته، وإن قال: خرج بأحديهما. فالأخرى إذا لم تخرج بها عن المكان الأول فلم تكن حركة، وإن قال: خرج بكل واحد منهما. قلنا: فإذا خرج بما لولا هو لما انعدم الخروج، والخروج بمثل هذا عين معقول، إذ العلل العقلية موجبات بذواتها فما يتصور ثبوت معلول بدونه، ولم ينعدم المعلول لو انعدم هو لا يكون علة بالثبوت، ولو كان لما كان به فكانت إحداهما غير موجبة للخروج فلم تكن حركة. يحققه : أن هذا الجزء ما قطع إلا مكانا وحدا، ولو جاز لك أن تقول: وجدت حركتان لوجود محركين كان لغيرك أن يقول : لا بل وجدت حركة لاتحاد المكان الذي قطع ويقال له: لو جاز وجود حركتين لا يقطع بهما إلا مكان واحد لجاز وجود ألف حركة لا يقطع بهما إلا مكان واحد، وهو يلتزم هنا. ويقول: لو حرك الجسم ألف نفر وأكثر حدث في كل جزء من أجزائه من الحركات بعدد الفاعلين، والقول بوجود ألف حركة لا يقطع بها إلا مكان واحد تجاهل، ولو جاز أن يخطر أحد هذا بباله لجاز لغيره أن يقول على القلب، ويجوز أن يقطع ألف مكان بحركة واحدة. وهذا كله هذيان، فاقتضت بهم أصولهم الفاسدة إلى أن جوزوا تارة قيام عرض واحد بألف محل وأكثر، وجوزوا تارة قيام ألف عرض من جنس واحد وأكثر بمحل لا أثر لها إلا ما لواحد منها، وهذا كله محال. ومن دأب المعتزلة عدم المبالاة بالانسلاخ عن الدين، وارتكاب ما يأباه العقل وينادي بإحالته ويحكم على قائله بالتجاهل والخروج عن المعارف عند رجائهم نصرة ما هم عليه من الباطل، ودفع ما يتوجه عليهم من الحجج الهادفة لقواعد ما هم عليه من الضلال الآتية على ما يتمسكون به من البدع بالإبطال والاستئصال والرجوع إلى الطريق المستبين والصراط المستقيم خير من الإمعان في المهاوي والمهالك والإيجاف في البوادي والمجاهل، ونعوذ بالله.
And Hisham ibn 'Amr claimed that each part of the stone contains two motions, one being the act of this [agent] and the other the act of that [agent]. This is impossible, because if the part exits the first location by one of them, then it is more fitting [that it does so] if it does not exit by it from the first location, then it would not be a motion; and if it does not exit by one of them from the first location, then it is not a motion. If he says: 'It exits by one of them when it is alone, and by both when they are combined.' We say: Does the part exit the first location by both of them together, or by one of them, or by each one of them? If he says: 'It exits by both of them together,' then both of them together are one cause, and each one of them is part of the cause, and this is false, because it would not be its motion. If he says: 'It exits by one of them,' then the other, since it does not cause exit from the first location, is not a motion. If he says: 'It exits by each one of them.' We say: Then it exits by that which, were it not for it, the exit would not be absent; and exit by such a thing is clearly rational, for intellectual causes necessitate by themselves, so what can have an effect subsist without it? And if the effect were not absent were it to be absent, it would not be a cause in subsistence; and if it were, then it would not be by it, so one of them would not necessitate exit and thus would not be a motion. This is confirmed: that this part only traversed a single location; and if you were allowed to say: 'Two motions exist because two movers exist,' then another could say: 'No, rather one motion exists because of the unity of the location traversed.' And it is said to him: If it were possible for two motions to exist by which only one location is traversed, then it would be possible for a thousand motions to exist by which only one location is traversed, and he commits to that. And he says: If a thousand or more persons move a body, there would occur in each of its parts motions equal to the number of agents. And the statement that a thousand motions exist by which only one location is traversed is ignorance; and if it were possible for anyone to entertain this in his mind, then it would be possible for another to say the opposite, and it would be possible to traverse a thousand locations by a single motion. All of this is nonsense. Their corrupt principles led them sometimes to allow one accident to subsist in a thousand loci or more, and sometimes to allow a thousand accidents of one genus or more to subsist in a locus with no effect other than what one of them would have. All this is impossible. It is the habit of the Mu'tazila to have no concern for stripping themselves of religion, and to commit what reason rejects and declares impossible, and which judges its speaker to be ignorant and outside of knowledge, when they hope to support the falsehood they follow and to repel the conclusive arguments that destroy the foundations of their error and come to annihilate and uproot the innovations they cling to. Returning to the clear path and the straight way is better than plunging into precipices and destructions and floundering in deserts and ignorances. We seek refuge with Allah.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim of Hisham ibn 'Amr that each particle of a stone contains two motions from two different agents. The author argues by analyzing whether the particle exits its original location by one or both motions. If it exits by one, the other is not a motion; if by both, they together are one cause, making each a partial cause, which is invalid. A third possibility (each independently) leads to a contradiction because the exit would depend on each, implying both are necessary but then neither alone suffices. The absurdity escalates: if two motions can traverse one location, then a thousand can do the same, and conversely one motion could traverse a thousand locations. The author attributes such errors to the Mu'tazila's corrupt principles, which allow one accident in many loci or many accidents of the same kind in one locus with no combined effect. The author concludes with a strong condemnation and a call to return to the straight path.

Key Terms
جزء
حركتان
محرك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That a particle can have two independent motions from two agents without contradiction.
Correction: Nasafi shows that for a motion to be real, it must produce an effect (exit from location). If one motion already produces the effect, the other is redundant or nonexistent.

Checkpoint
What is the key criterion Nasafi uses to define a real motion?
A) The motion must be visible.
B) The motion must cause the particle to exit its location.
C) The motion must be caused by an external agent.
D) The motion must be continuous.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi's initial argument shows that the claim of two motions in one particle reduces to absurdity because each motion must either move the particle or not, leading to contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever attribute your spiritual progress or failure to multiple causes—your effort, another person's influence, divine decree—without considering that only one true cause ultimately moves you? Will you examine your heart today and ask Allah to purify your intention, acknowledging that He alone is the real mover?
?
This lesson shows that contradictory 'motions' cannot coexist in a simple particle. What contradictory desires or beliefs do you harbor in your heart—such as love of this world and love of the Hereafter? Are you willing to let one of them die so that the other can be real?
?
Hisham's claim is refuted because it defies logical necessity. Is there any belief you hold that, when scrutinized, relies on a similar contradiction? Will you commit to abandoning it, no matter how comfortable, for the sake of tawhid?

The Dialogue: Three Possibilities Examined
Nasafi presents a dialogue refuting three ways Hisham might explain the combined motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's response to Hisham's attempted solution that the particle exits by one motion when alone and by both when combined.

Core Idea
Hisham's attempt to combine the motions fails under logical analysis of causality.

Hisham responds to the dilemma by claiming that the particle exits by one motion when that motion is alone, but by both when they are together. Nasafi then poses three questions to test this, each leading to a contradiction. This lesson explores the logical dissection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the dialogue between Nasafi and Hisham.
2
Identify the three possibilities
Nasafi asks: does the particle exit by both together, by one of them, or by each? Note how each is refuted.
The third possibility is particularly subtle.
3
Understand the causal principle
Nasafi invokes the principle that intellectual causes necessitate by themselves. If each motion independently causes exit, then the exit would depend on both, which is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم هشام بن عمرو أن كل جزء من أجزاء الحجر يحصل فيه حركتان أحداهما فعل لهذا والأخرى فعل لذلك، وهذا محال، لأن الجزاء إن كان يخرج بأحديهما عن المكان الأول فالأحرى إذا لم تخرج بها عن المكان الأول فلا تكون حركة، وإن كان لا يخرج بأحديهما عن المكان الأول فهى ليست بحركة. فإن قال: يخرج بأحديهما إذا انفردت وبهما إذا اجتمعت. قلنا: إذا خرج الجزء بهما عن المكان الأول أخرج بهما جميعًا أم بأحديهما أم بكل واحد منهما؟ فإن قال : خرج بهما جميعًا فهما جميعًا علة واحدة فكانت كل واحدة منهما بعض العلة وهو باطل، لأنها لم تكن حركته، وإن قال: خرج بأحديهما. فالأخرى إذا لم تخرج بها عن المكان الأول فلم تكن حركة، وإن قال: خرج بكل واحد منهما. قلنا: فإذا خرج بما لولا هو لما انعدم الخروج، والخروج بمثل هذا عين معقول، إذ العلل العقلية موجبات بذواتها فما يتصور ثبوت معلول بدونه، ولم ينعدم المعلول لو انعدم هو لا يكون علة بالثبوت، ولو كان لما كان به فكانت إحداهما غير موجبة للخروج فلم تكن حركة. يحققه : أن هذا الجزء ما قطع إلا مكانا وحدا، ولو جاز لك أن تقول: وجدت حركتان لوجود محركين كان لغيرك أن يقول : لا بل وجدت حركة لاتحاد المكان الذي قطع ويقال له: لو جاز وجود حركتين لا يقطع بهما إلا مكان واحد لجاز وجود ألف حركة لا يقطع بهما إلا مكان واحد، وهو يلتزم هنا. ويقول: لو حرك الجسم ألف نفر وأكثر حدث في كل جزء من أجزائه من الحركات بعدد الفاعلين، والقول بوجود ألف حركة لا يقطع بها إلا مكان واحد تجاهل، ولو جاز أن يخطر أحد هذا بباله لجاز لغيره أن يقول على القلب، ويجوز أن يقطع ألف مكان بحركة واحدة. وهذا كله هذيان، فاقتضت بهم أصولهم الفاسدة إلى أن جوزوا تارة قيام عرض واحد بألف محل وأكثر، وجوزوا تارة قيام ألف عرض من جنس واحد وأكثر بمحل لا أثر لها إلا ما لواحد منها، وهذا كله محال. ومن دأب المعتزلة عدم المبالاة بالانسلاخ عن الدين، وارتكاب ما يأباه العقل وينادي بإحالته ويحكم على قائله بالتجاهل والخروج عن المعارف عند رجائهم نصرة ما هم عليه من الباطل، ودفع ما يتوجه عليهم من الحجج الهادفة لقواعد ما هم عليه من الضلال الآتية على ما يتمسكون به من البدع بالإبطال والاستئصال والرجوع إلى الطريق المستبين والصراط المستقيم خير من الإمعان في المهاوي والمهالك والإيجاف في البوادي والمجاهل، ونعوذ بالله.
And Hisham ibn 'Amr claimed that each part of the stone contains two motions, one being the act of this [agent] and the other the act of that [agent]. This is impossible, because if the part exits the first location by one of them, then it is more fitting [that it does so] if it does not exit by it from the first location, then it would not be a motion; and if it does not exit by one of them from the first location, then it is not a motion. If he says: 'It exits by one of them when it is alone, and by both when they are combined.' We say: Does the part exit the first location by both of them together, or by one of them, or by each one of them? If he says: 'It exits by both of them together,' then both of them together are one cause, and each one of them is part of the cause, and this is false, because it would not be its motion. If he says: 'It exits by one of them,' then the other, since it does not cause exit from the first location, is not a motion. If he says: 'It exits by each one of them.' We say: Then it exits by that which, were it not for it, the exit would not be absent; and exit by such a thing is clearly rational, for intellectual causes necessitate by themselves, so what can have an effect subsist without it? And if the effect were not absent were it to be absent, it would not be a cause in subsistence; and if it were, then it would not be by it, so one of them would not necessitate exit and thus would not be a motion. This is confirmed: that this part only traversed a single location; and if you were allowed to say: 'Two motions exist because two movers exist,' then another could say: 'No, rather one motion exists because of the unity of the location traversed.' And it is said to him: If it were possible for two motions to exist by which only one location is traversed, then it would be possible for a thousand motions to exist by which only one location is traversed, and he commits to that. And he says: If a thousand or more persons move a body, there would occur in each of its parts motions equal to the number of agents. And the statement that a thousand motions exist by which only one location is traversed is ignorance; and if it were possible for anyone to entertain this in his mind, then it would be possible for another to say the opposite, and it would be possible to traverse a thousand locations by a single motion. All of this is nonsense. Their corrupt principles led them sometimes to allow one accident to subsist in a thousand loci or more, and sometimes to allow a thousand accidents of one genus or more to subsist in a locus with no effect other than what one of them would have. All this is impossible. It is the habit of the Mu'tazila to have no concern for stripping themselves of religion, and to commit what reason rejects and declares impossible, and which judges its speaker to be ignorant and outside of knowledge, when they hope to support the falsehood they follow and to repel the conclusive arguments that destroy the foundations of their error and come to annihilate and uproot the innovations they cling to. Returning to the clear path and the straight way is better than plunging into precipices and destructions and floundering in deserts and ignorances. We seek refuge with Allah.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim of Hisham ibn 'Amr that each particle of a stone contains two motions from two different agents. The author argues by analyzing whether the particle exits its original location by one or both motions. If it exits by one, the other is not a motion; if by both, they together are one cause, making each a partial cause, which is invalid. A third possibility (each independently) leads to a contradiction because the exit would depend on each, implying both are necessary but then neither alone suffices. The absurdity escalates: if two motions can traverse one location, then a thousand can do the same, and conversely one motion could traverse a thousand locations. The author attributes such errors to the Mu'tazila's corrupt principles, which allow one accident in many loci or many accidents of the same kind in one locus with no combined effect. The author concludes with a strong condemnation and a call to return to the straight path.

Key Terms
علة
موجب
معلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the principle Nasafi uses to refute the third possibility (exit by each motion)?
A) Motion is indivisible.
B) Causes necessitate their effects by themselves.
C) Two causes cannot act on one object.
D) A particle cannot have two motions.

Key Takeaway
Hisham's attempt to combine motions fails because each logical possibility leads to a contradiction regarding causation and the unity of the effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you try to explain why something happens in your life (like a habit or a trial), do you ever settle for a comfortable but logically flawed explanation because it feels right? How can you train yourself to demand the same logical rigor that Nasafi demanded of Hisham?
?
This passage shows that combining two insufficient causes doesn't make a sufficient one. In your own acts of worship or character development, do you sometimes rely on multiple partial efforts hoping they add up to something real, while each alone is empty? What would it mean for one cause to be truly sufficient in your relationship with Allah?
?
Nasafi uses the principle that a cause necessitates its effect. If you truly believed that Allah is the sole cause of everything, how would it change the way you plan your day or react to outcomes? Are there areas where you still think something else shares that causal power?

The Reductio ad Absurdum and Critique of Mu'tazili Principles
Nasafi extends the argument with a reductio and then attacks the Mu'tazili foundations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi extends the refutation to a general reductio and condemns the Mu'tazili approach as leading to absurdities.

Core Idea
If two motions can traverse one location, then any number of motions could, and the Mu'tazila's principles allow incoherent accidents.

Nasafi now pushes the argument to its extreme consequences. If two motions can occupy the same particle, why not a thousand? And conversely, one motion could traverse a thousand locations. He then criticizes the underlying Mu'tazili principles that allow one accident in many loci or many accidents of one kind in one locus with no combined effect. This lesson shows the broader implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the reductio and the critique. Notice how Nasafi uses escalation to show absurdity.
2
Understand the reductio
He argues that if two motions can traverse one space, then a thousand motions can also traverse one space, which is obviously false. Similarly, the reverse claim leads to absurdity.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
3
Analyze the broader critique
Nasafi attributes these errors to Mu'tazili principles that allow accidents to have no proportional effect. He condemns their disregard for reason and religion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم هشام بن عمرو أن كل جزء من أجزاء الحجر يحصل فيه حركتان أحداهما فعل لهذا والأخرى فعل لذلك، وهذا محال، لأن الجزاء إن كان يخرج بأحديهما عن المكان الأول فالأحرى إذا لم تخرج بها عن المكان الأول فلا تكون حركة، وإن كان لا يخرج بأحديهما عن المكان الأول فهى ليست بحركة. فإن قال: يخرج بأحديهما إذا انفردت وبهما إذا اجتمعت. قلنا: إذا خرج الجزء بهما عن المكان الأول أخرج بهما جميعًا أم بأحديهما أم بكل واحد منهما؟ فإن قال : خرج بهما جميعًا فهما جميعًا علة واحدة فكانت كل واحدة منهما بعض العلة وهو باطل، لأنها لم تكن حركته، وإن قال: خرج بأحديهما. فالأخرى إذا لم تخرج بها عن المكان الأول فلم تكن حركة، وإن قال: خرج بكل واحد منهما. قلنا: فإذا خرج بما لولا هو لما انعدم الخروج، والخروج بمثل هذا عين معقول، إذ العلل العقلية موجبات بذواتها فما يتصور ثبوت معلول بدونه، ولم ينعدم المعلول لو انعدم هو لا يكون علة بالثبوت، ولو كان لما كان به فكانت إحداهما غير موجبة للخروج فلم تكن حركة. يحققه : أن هذا الجزء ما قطع إلا مكانا وحدا، ولو جاز لك أن تقول: وجدت حركتان لوجود محركين كان لغيرك أن يقول : لا بل وجدت حركة لاتحاد المكان الذي قطع ويقال له: لو جاز وجود حركتين لا يقطع بهما إلا مكان واحد لجاز وجود ألف حركة لا يقطع بهما إلا مكان واحد، وهو يلتزم هنا. ويقول: لو حرك الجسم ألف نفر وأكثر حدث في كل جزء من أجزائه من الحركات بعدد الفاعلين، والقول بوجود ألف حركة لا يقطع بها إلا مكان واحد تجاهل، ولو جاز أن يخطر أحد هذا بباله لجاز لغيره أن يقول على القلب، ويجوز أن يقطع ألف مكان بحركة واحدة. وهذا كله هذيان، فاقتضت بهم أصولهم الفاسدة إلى أن جوزوا تارة قيام عرض واحد بألف محل وأكثر، وجوزوا تارة قيام ألف عرض من جنس واحد وأكثر بمحل لا أثر لها إلا ما لواحد منها، وهذا كله محال. ومن دأب المعتزلة عدم المبالاة بالانسلاخ عن الدين، وارتكاب ما يأباه العقل وينادي بإحالته ويحكم على قائله بالتجاهل والخروج عن المعارف عند رجائهم نصرة ما هم عليه من الباطل، ودفع ما يتوجه عليهم من الحجج الهادفة لقواعد ما هم عليه من الضلال الآتية على ما يتمسكون به من البدع بالإبطال والاستئصال والرجوع إلى الطريق المستبين والصراط المستقيم خير من الإمعان في المهاوي والمهالك والإيجاف في البوادي والمجاهل، ونعوذ بالله.
And Hisham ibn 'Amr claimed that each part of the stone contains two motions, one being the act of this [agent] and the other the act of that [agent]. This is impossible, because if the part exits the first location by one of them, then it is more fitting [that it does so] if it does not exit by it from the first location, then it would not be a motion; and if it does not exit by one of them from the first location, then it is not a motion. If he says: 'It exits by one of them when it is alone, and by both when they are combined.' We say: Does the part exit the first location by both of them together, or by one of them, or by each one of them? If he says: 'It exits by both of them together,' then both of them together are one cause, and each one of them is part of the cause, and this is false, because it would not be its motion. If he says: 'It exits by one of them,' then the other, since it does not cause exit from the first location, is not a motion. If he says: 'It exits by each one of them.' We say: Then it exits by that which, were it not for it, the exit would not be absent; and exit by such a thing is clearly rational, for intellectual causes necessitate by themselves, so what can have an effect subsist without it? And if the effect were not absent were it to be absent, it would not be a cause in subsistence; and if it were, then it would not be by it, so one of them would not necessitate exit and thus would not be a motion. This is confirmed: that this part only traversed a single location; and if you were allowed to say: 'Two motions exist because two movers exist,' then another could say: 'No, rather one motion exists because of the unity of the location traversed.' And it is said to him: If it were possible for two motions to exist by which only one location is traversed, then it would be possible for a thousand motions to exist by which only one location is traversed, and he commits to that. And he says: If a thousand or more persons move a body, there would occur in each of its parts motions equal to the number of agents. And the statement that a thousand motions exist by which only one location is traversed is ignorance; and if it were possible for anyone to entertain this in his mind, then it would be possible for another to say the opposite, and it would be possible to traverse a thousand locations by a single motion. All of this is nonsense. Their corrupt principles led them sometimes to allow one accident to subsist in a thousand loci or more, and sometimes to allow a thousand accidents of one genus or more to subsist in a locus with no effect other than what one of them would have. All this is impossible. It is the habit of the Mu'tazila to have no concern for stripping themselves of religion, and to commit what reason rejects and declares impossible, and which judges its speaker to be ignorant and outside of knowledge, when they hope to support the falsehood they follow and to repel the conclusive arguments that destroy the foundations of their error and come to annihilate and uproot the innovations they cling to. Returning to the clear path and the straight way is better than plunging into precipices and destructions and floundering in deserts and ignorances. We seek refuge with Allah.

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim of Hisham ibn 'Amr that each particle of a stone contains two motions from two different agents. The author argues by analyzing whether the particle exits its original location by one or both motions. If it exits by one, the other is not a motion; if by both, they together are one cause, making each a partial cause, which is invalid. A third possibility (each independently) leads to a contradiction because the exit would depend on each, implying both are necessary but then neither alone suffices. The author attributes such errors to the Mu'tazila's corrupt principles, which allow one accident in many loci or many accidents of the same kind in one locus with no combined effect. The author concludes with a strong condemnation and a call to return to the straight path.

Checkpoint
What logical consequence does Nasafi derive from Hisham's claim?
A) Two motions would require two separate particles.
B) If two motions can traverse one location, then a thousand can, and conversely one motion could traverse a thousand locations.
C) Motion is eternal.
D) The particle would split into two.

Key Takeaway
Hisham's claim, if accepted, leads to limitless absurdities, revealing the corrupt principles of the Mu'tazila that allow effects without proportional causes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life are you clinging to a belief or practice that, if honestly examined, would collapse into absurdity? What would it cost you to abandon it and return to the clear path?
?

?
Imagine your own reasoning leads to a conclusion that contradicts sound principles. Would you have the humility to admit error, or would you, like the Mu'tazila, persist in defending falsehood? What false principles might you be protecting today?

The Verbal Difference Over Human Action
The author argues the difference is verbal but critiques the deeper Mu'tazili error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Maturidi-Mu'tazili disagreement on human action is essentially verbal, but the Mu'tazili position leads to theological errors that undermine divine omnipotence.

Core Idea
The difference is in words, but the Mu'tazila's error goes beyond words.

This passage presents a crucial argument by Imam al-Nasafi that the conflict between the Maturidis and Mu'tazila over human action is more about terminology than substance. However, he warns that the Mu'tazili terminology leads them to deny divine omnipotence, aligning them with materialist thought. Let us read the passage carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the claim
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the author's opening statement that the difference is only in expression.
Pay attention to the words 'خلق' (creation) and 'كسب' (acquisition).
2
Understand the scope of agreement
The author says both sides agree on the extent of the servant's power. The only difference is what they call it. Identify that common ground.
3
Examine the deeper critique
Read the part where the author criticizes the Mu'tazila for restricting power to existence, which leads to absurdity. Understand why this is a serious error.
The author claims this makes them like materialists (دهرية) and negators (معطلة).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وراء الشيئية، فينبغي أن لا تتعلق قدرة العبد به فلم يمكنهم تعليق قدرة العبد إلا بقدر ما قلنا، فإذا قلنا بمثل ما قالوا ولم يبق بيننا خلاف إلا في العبارة فإنهم سموا ذلك خلقًا واختراعا، ونحن سميناه كسبًا إلا أن ما وراء ذلك عندنا متعلق بقدرة الله تعالى وعندهم لا يقدره أحد فاستوينا في جنبة العبد ولم يبق لهم علينا إشكال، وفيما وراء ذلك التحقوا بالدهرية والمعطلة، ونحن ثبنا على القول بثبوت الصانع بل هم أتوا بما هو غير المعقول وأبطلوا القول بتعلق القدرة بالمقدور، فإنهم أحالوا تعلقها إلا بالوجود والوجود راجع إلى الذات إذ هو ليس بمعنى وراء الذات ولا تعلق لها بالذات والشيئية فإن تعلقها بما لا تعلق لها به وهو محال وهذيان وبطل بهذا الفصل جميع قواعد المعتزلة وأضمحلت شبهاتهم، ونحن نحمد الله في غاية الوضوح.
Beyond thing-ness, so the power of the servant should not be attached to it, so they could not attach the power of the servant except to the extent we said. So when we say like what they said, and no difference remains between us except in expression—for they called that creation and invention, and we called it acquisition—except that what is beyond that is with us attached to the power of Allah, and with them no one can bring it about. So we are equal regarding the servant, and no difficulty remains for us against them. And in what is beyond that, they join the materialists and the negators, while we remain upon the statement affirming the Maker. Rather, they brought what is inconceivable and invalidated the statement that power is attached to the possible. For they deemed its attachment impossible except to existence, and existence returns to essence since it is not a meaning beyond the essence, and there is no attachment of power to the essence and thing-ness. So its attachment to that to which it has no attachment is impossible and nonsense. And by this chapter, all the principles of the Mu'tazila are invalidated and their doubts are dissolved, and we praise Allah in utmost clarity.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents the core argument that the difference between the Maturidi position and the Mu'tazili position is merely verbal regarding human action. The author states that both sides agree that the servant's power is attached to something limited, but the Mu'tazila call that 'creation' while the Sunnis call it 'acquisition'. Beyond that, concerning the origin of the action, the Sunnis attribute it to Allah's power, while the Mu'tazila deny any power over it, thus falling into the position of materialists who deny a creator. The author then critiques the Mu'tazili claim that power is only attached to existence, arguing that existence is not distinct from essence, so this leads to absurdity. The passage concludes that all Mu'tazili principles are invalidated.

Key Terms
الشيئية
القدرة
الكسب
الاختراع
الدهرية
المعطلة
الصانع
الوجود
الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The difference between Maturidis and Mu'tazila is only a trivial matter of wording.
Correction: Although the difference is verbal, the Mu'tazili wording implies a denial of divine power over the action, which leads to a serious theological error that undermines tawhid.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the real difference between the Maturidi and Mu'tazili positions on human action?
A) It is only in expression.
B) The Mu'tazila deny divine power entirely.
C) The Maturidis deny human power entirely.
D) There is no difference.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi position preserves both divine omnipotence and human accountability, while the Mu'tazili position, if followed logically, leads to denying the Creator's power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own actions, do you truly believe that every detail—including your ability to act—is from Allah? Or is there a part of your heart that feels you independently 'create' your own deeds?
?
The Mu'tazila thought they were defending God's justice, but ended up denying His power. Are there any beliefs you hold that, if followed to their logical end, would subtly undermine your reliance on Allah's absolute sovereignty?
?
If the only difference between you and someone who denies the Creator is a matter of words, how carefully do you guard your language about Allah's power and your own responsibility? Will you commit to affirming in your heart that every breath is from Him alone?

The Fourfold Dilemma of 'Invention'
The author subjects the meaning of 'invention' to a fourfold logical dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi scholar uses a fourfold logical dilemma to expose the incoherence of the Mu'tazili concept of invention.

Core Idea
Invention cannot be a coherent object of power; it leads to contradiction.

The Mu'tazila claim that human power is 'over invention'. But what exactly is invention? The Maturidi author forces them to define it. He systematically examines every possible definition and shows that each contradicts their own principles. This passage is a masterclass in logical refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the English translation. Let the rhythm of the dilemma sink in.
Notice the four-fold structure: existent, non-existent, both, neither.
2
Identify the four possibilities
The author lists four possible definitions for 'invention'. Write them down as you find them in the text.
3
Observe how each is refuted
For each possibility, the author points out an impossibility based on Mu'tazili own principles. Track which principle is violated.
For 'existent': power cannot attach to existent. For 'non-existent': attributes in non-existence cannot be attached to power. For 'both': contradiction. For 'neither': inconceivable.
4
Understand the Bāṭiniyya comparison
The author compares the fourth possibility to the Bāṭiniyya who say God is neither existent nor non-existent, which leads to atheism and sophistry. This shows the danger of such a definition.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how this dilemma undermines the Mu'tazili claim that human power is over invention. Is the concept of invention salvageable?
The lesson is that without a coherent definition, the claim is baseless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول ما معنى قولكم: إن قدرتنا قدرة على الاختراع؟ وما هذا الاختراع الذي تزعمون أن قدرتكم متعلقة به أهو اسم لموجود أم لمعدوم وموجود أم لا لموجود ولا لمعدوم؟. فإن قلتم : إنه اسم لموجود، فهو محال عندكم لأن تعلق القدرة بالموجود عندكم محال، وإن قلتم : إنه اسم لمعدوم، فهو محال أيضا، لأنه يوجب أن يكون في العدم اختراع وكل وصف كان في العدم ثابتا كان تعلق القدرة به محالاً كالشيئية والجوهر والعرضية والعينية وغير ذلك من الأوصاف الثابتة في العدم عندكم، وإن قلتم إنه اسم للموجود والمعدوم فهذا كلام متناقض، وإن قلتم إنه اسم لا لموجود ولا لمعدوم فهو اسم لما لا يعقل إذ لا يتصور معلوم ليس بموجود ولا معدوم، وهذا من جهالات الباطنية فإنهم يزعمون أن الباري عز وجل ليس بموجود ولا معدوم، وهذا قول يؤدي إلى الإلحاد والسفسطة، والله الموفق.
Then we say: What is the meaning of your statement: 'Our power is a power over invention'? And what is this invention which you claim your power is attached to? Is it a name for an existent or for a non-existent, or for both existent and non-existent, or for neither existent nor non-existent? For if you say: It is a name for an existent, then it is impossible according to you because attachment of power to the existent is impossible according to you. And if you say: It is a name for a non-existent, it is also impossible, because it necessitates that in non-existence there be invention, and every attribute that is established in non-existence, the attachment of power to it is impossible—like thing-ness, substance, being an accident, being an entity, and other attributes established in non-existence according to you. And if you say it is a name for the existent and the non-existent, then this is contradictory speech. And if you say it is a name for neither existent nor non-existent, then it is a name for what is inconceivable, for there is no conceivable known thing that is neither existent nor non-existent. And this is from the ignorances of the Bāṭiniyya, for they claim that the Creator, may He be exalted, is neither existent nor non-existent. And this statement leads to atheism and sophistry. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a logical refutation of the Mu'tazili concept of 'invention'. The Maturidi author asks what this invention is as a name. He presents four possibilities: it is a name for an existent, a non-existent, both, or neither. For each, he points out contradictions based on the Mu'tazila's own doctrines. If it is an existent, they claim power cannot attach to an existent. If non-existent, then invention would be in non-existence, which is impossible. If both, contradiction. If neither, then it is inconceivable, akin to the Bāṭiniyya who say God is neither existent nor non-existent, which leads to atheism. Thus, the Mu'tazili claim is incoherent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Invention is a self-evident concept that can be defined unambiguously.
Correction: The passage demonstrates that every attempt to define invention leads to contradiction, so it is not a coherent concept at all.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the possibilities considered for the meaning of 'invention'?
A) Name for an existent.
B) Name for a non-existent.
C) Name for a contingent being.
D) Name for neither existent nor non-existent.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili concept of 'invention' cannot be consistently defined, rendering their claim of power over invention logically untenable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author calls the view that something can be neither existent nor non-existent 'ignorance' leading to atheism. Search your own heart: have you ever held a belief about Allah or about reality that you could not logically define? Are you willing to abandon any incoherent thought, even if it feels comfortable? Write down one such belief you need to correct.
?
This passage forces the Mu‘tazila to define 'invention' and shows every definition fails. What areas of your own faith or practice have you left undefined, hoping they would 'just make sense'? Commit today to seeking clear, sound knowledge from the Qur’an and Sunnah, even if it means dismantling a cherished idea.
?
The author warns that a vague concept leads to sophistry (denial of truth). Think of a time when you used vague religious language to avoid a hard question. Will you now face that question with the clarity this lesson demands, or will you continue in ambiguity? Resolve to pursue truth over comfort.

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
5 min
Turning the Mu'tazili Objection Back
Response to Mu'tazili objection by turning it back.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi response uses the Mu'tazila's own principles to reverse the objection about God creating motion.

Core Idea
The Maturidi turns the Mu'tazili question back by asking: what do you do, if God does not create the substance?

This passage presents a clever dialectical argument. A Mu'tazili objection is turned inside out: they ask 'if God creates motion, what do I do?' The author responds by showing that, according to their own denial of human power over existence, they cannot explain what the human does either. The counter-question becomes a proof for the Maturidi position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Notice the structure: the objection and the response.
The argument is concise; pay attention to the logical flow.
2
Identify the objection and the counter-question
Locate the Mu'tazili objection: 'If Allah performs motion, what did I do?' Then find the author's counter-question: 'If you did not do the thing nor the entity, and God did not do the substance, accident, etc., then what did you do?'
The counter-question mirrors the structure of the objection.
3
Understand the logical twist
The author assumes the Mu'tazila's own principle: existence is identical to the entity, and God alone creates existence. So if God does not create the entities (substance, accident, etc.), neither does the human. Thus the Mu'tazila's answer to the counter-question also applies to their original objection.
This shows the objection is self-defeating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا يجابون عن قولهم: إن الله تعالى إذا فعل الحركة فماذا فعلت أنا ؟ فيقال لهم وإذا لم تفعل أنت الشيء ولا العين والوجود هو عين الشيء إذ ليس بمعنى وراءه فماذا فعلت إذا لم يفعل الله الجوهر ولا العرض ولا الشيء ولا العين ولا السواد ولا البياض ولا الرائحة ولا الطعم فماذا فعل؟ ووجودها إذا لم يكن معنى وراءها أو هو عينها وذاتها ولم يفعل عينها ولا ذاتها فماذا فعل؟ فما أجابوا من شيء فهو لهم جواب.
And with this they are answered regarding their statement: 'If Allah performs motion, then what did I do?' So it is said to them: And if you did not do the thing nor the entity—and existence is the very entity of the thing since it is not a meaning beyond it—then what did you do if Allah did not do the substance, nor the accident, nor the thing, nor the entity, nor blackness, nor whiteness, nor odor, nor taste? So what did He do? And if their existence is not a meaning beyond them, or He is the very entity and essence of them, and He did not do their entity nor their essence, then what did He do? So whatever they answer to something, it is an answer for them.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage provides a response to a specific Mu'tazili objection: 'If God creates motion, what do I do?' The author turns the question back on them. He argues that according to the Mu'tazila's own denial that anything besides God has power over existence, and since existence is the same as the entity, then if God does not create the substance, accident, thing, entity, blackness, etc., then neither did the human. So the Mu'tazila cannot explain what the human allegedly does. Whatever they answer, the same logic applies to the Maturidi position.

Key Terms
الحركة
الشيء
العين
الوجود
الجوهر
العرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazili objection that 'if God creates motion, the human does nothing' is unanswerable.
Correction: The author answers by turning the question back, showing the Mu'tazila cannot explain human action either, given their own principles.

Checkpoint
How does the author respond to the Mu'tazili question, 'If God creates motion, what did I do?'
A) He agrees that the human does nothing.
B) He argues that the human's act is the motion itself.
C) He turns it back by asking what the human did if God did not create the substance and accident.
D) He says the question is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi response to the Mu'tazili objection about God creating motion is to reverse the question, showing the Mu'tazila cannot explain human action either.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly feel that God created that sin, or do you instinctively claim ownership of the act? How does this passage challenge your hidden assumption that some actions are entirely yours?
?
If God does not create the very entity of your good deeds, then what have you actually done? Can you point to any action in your life that is entirely your own creation? Let this question sit until it unsettles you.
?
The Mu'tazila claimed humans create their own acts to preserve divine justice. But the Maturidi turns their logic back: you create nothing at all. Does this make God unjust? Or does it reveal that your concept of justice needs to be redefined by the truth of God's absolute sovereignty?
